<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ko</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">kua</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">kua</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ko</span></td>
<td>'melon'
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span lang="zh">下</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ɕia</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ɕiɑ</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">xo</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ɦo</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ɦo</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ɦo</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ia</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">xa</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ɣo</span></td>
<td>'down'
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Nantongnese has heavy Wu influence, which has led to it also having raised and backed vowels.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Danzhou_dialect" title="Danzhou dialect">Danzhounese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maihua" title="Maihua">Maihua</a> are both traditionally considered <a href="/wiki/Yue_Chinese" title="Yue Chinese">Yue</a> lects.<sup id="cite_ref-atlas_21-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atlas-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Recent research, however, has noted that these are both are more likely unclassified.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKurpaska201073_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKurpaska201073-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Maihua, for example, may be a Yue-<a href="/wiki/Hakka_Chinese" title="Hakka Chinese">Hakka</a>-<a href="/wiki/Hainanese_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Hainanese language">Hainanese Min</a> mixed language.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Dongjiang Bendihua (<span lang="zh">東江本地話</span>) is spoken in and around <a href="/wiki/Huizhou" title="Huizhou">Huizhou</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heyuan" title="Heyuan">Heyuan</a>. Its classification has always been unclear, though the most common standpoint is that it is considered Hakka.<sup id="cite_ref-atlas_21-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atlas-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Northern_China">Northern China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinitic_languages&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Northern China"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The variety spoken in the <a href="/wiki/Ganyu_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Ganyu District">Ganyu District</a> of <a href="/wiki/Lianyungang" title="Lianyungang">Lianyungang</a> (<span lang="zh">贛榆話</span>) is listed as a variety of <a href="/wiki/Central_Plains_Mandarin" title="Central Plains Mandarin">Central Plains Mandarin</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Language_Atlas_of_China" title="Language Atlas of China">Language Atlas of China</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-atlas_21-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atlas-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> though its tonal distribution is more similar to <a href="/wiki/Jiao-Liao_Mandarin" class="mw-redirect" title="Jiao-Liao Mandarin">Peninsular Mandarin</a> varieties.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relationships_between_groups">Relationships between groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinitic_languages&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Relationships between groups"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Jerry_Norman_(sinologist)" title="Jerry Norman (sinologist)">Jerry Norman</a> classified the traditional seven dialect groups into three larger groups: Northern (Mandarin), Central (Wu, Gan, and Xiang) and Southern (Hakka, Yue, and Min). He argued that the Southern Group is derived from a standard used in the Yangtze valley during the <a href="/wiki/Han_dynasty" title="Han dynasty">Han dynasty</a> (206 BC&#160;&#8211;&#32;220 AD), which he called Old Southern Chinese, while the Central group was transitional between the Northern and Southern groups.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENorman1988182–183_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENorman1988182–183-71">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>  Some <a href="/wiki/Dialect_boundaries" class="mw-redirect" title="Dialect boundaries">dialect boundaries</a>, such as between Wu and Min, are particularly abrupt, while others, such as between Mandarin and Xiang or between Min and Hakka, are much less clearly defined.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENorman1988189–190_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENorman1988189–190-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Scholars account for the transitional nature of the central varieties in terms of <a href="/wiki/Wave_model" title="Wave model">wave models</a>. Iwata argues that innovations have been transmitted from the north across the <a href="/wiki/Huai_River" title="Huai River">Huai River</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Lower_Yangtze_Mandarin" title="Lower Yangtze Mandarin">Lower Yangtze Mandarin</a> area and from there southeast to the Wu area and westwards along the <a href="/wiki/Yangtze_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Yangtze River">Yangtze River</a> valley and thence to southwestern areas, leaving the hills of the southeast largely untouched.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIwata2010102–108_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIwata2010102–108-72">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A_quantitative_study">A quantitative study</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinitic_languages&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: A quantitative study"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A 2007 study compared fifteen major urban dialects on the objective criteria of <a href="/wiki/Lexical_similarity" title="Lexical similarity">lexical similarity</a> and regularity of sound correspondences, and subjective criteria of intelligibility and similarity.  Most of these criteria show a top-level split with Northern, <a href="/wiki/New_Xiang" title="New Xiang">New Xiang</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gan_Chinese" title="Gan Chinese">Gan</a> in one group and <a href="/wiki/Min_Chinese" title="Min Chinese">Min</a> (samples at Fuzhou, Xiamen, Chaozhou), <a href="/wiki/Hakka_Chinese" title="Hakka Chinese">Hakka</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yue_Chinese" title="Yue Chinese">Yue</a> in the other group.  The exception was phonological regularity, where the one Gan dialect (<a href="/wiki/Nanchang_Gan" class="mw-redirect" title="Nanchang Gan">Nanchang Gan</a>) was in the Southern group and very close to <a href="/wiki/Meixian_dialect" title="Meixian dialect">Meixian Hakka</a>, and the deepest phonological difference was between <a href="/wiki/Wenzhounese" title="Wenzhounese">Wenzhounese</a> (the southernmost Wu dialect) and all other dialects.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETangVan_Heuven20071025_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETangVan_Heuven20071025-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The study did not find clear splits within the Northern and Central areas:<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETangVan_Heuven20071025_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETangVan_Heuven20071025-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Changsha (New Xiang) was always within the Mandarin group. No Old Xiang dialect was in the sample.</li>
<li>Taiyuan (<a href="/wiki/Jin_Chinese" title="Jin Chinese">Jin</a> or Shanxi) and Hankou (Wuhan, Hubei) were subjectively perceived as relatively different from other Northern dialects but were very close in mutual intelligibility. Objectively, Taiyuan had substantial phonological divergence but little lexical divergence.</li>
<li>Chengdu (Sichuan) was somewhat divergent lexically but very little on the other measures.</li></ul>
<p>The two <a href="/wiki/Wu_dialect" class="mw-redirect" title="Wu dialect">Wu dialects</a> (Wenzhou and Suzhou) occupied an intermediate position, closer to the Northern/New Xiang/Gan group in lexical similarity and strongly closer in subjective intelligibility but closer to Min/Hakka/Yue in phonological regularity and subjective similarity, except that Wenzhou was farthest from all other dialects in phonological regularity. The two Wu dialects were close to each other in lexical similarity and subjective similarity but not in mutual intelligibility, where Suzhou was actually closer to Northern/Xiang/Gan than to Wenzhou.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETangVan_Heuven20071025_73-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETangVan_Heuven20071025-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the Southern subgroup, Hakka and Yue grouped closely together on the three lexical and subjective measures but not in phonological regularity.  The Min dialects showed high divergence, with Min Fuzhou (<a href="/wiki/Eastern_Min" title="Eastern Min">Eastern Min</a>) grouped only weakly with the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Min" title="Southern Min">Southern Min</a> dialects of <a href="/wiki/Amoy_dialect" title="Amoy dialect">Xiamen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Teochew_dialect" title="Teochew dialect">Chaozhou</a> on the two objective criteria and was actually slightly closer to Hakka and Yue on the subjective criteria.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETangVan_Heuven20071025_73-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETangVan_Heuven20071025-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Internal_comparison">Internal comparison</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinitic_languages&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Internal comparison"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The following section will be dedicated to compare non-Bai and non-Cai–Long Sinitic languages. Though all stem from Old Chinese, they have all developed differences with each other.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Writing_system">Writing system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinitic_languages&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Writing system"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Pa-khek-le_Kau-hoe.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="POJ inscription" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Pa-khek-le_Kau-hoe.jpg/220px-Pa-khek-le_Kau-hoe.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="128" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Pa-khek-le_Kau-hoe.jpg/330px-Pa-khek-le_Kau-hoe.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Pa-khek-le_Kau-hoe.jpg/440px-Pa-khek-le_Kau-hoe.jpg 2x" data-file-width="683" data-file-height="396" /></a><figcaption>An example of Hokkien written exclusively in the Latin alphabet.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Typographically, the vast majority of Sinitic languages use <a href="/wiki/Chinese_characters" title="Chinese characters">Sinographs</a>. However, some varieties, such as <a href="/wiki/Dungan_language" title="Dungan language">Dungan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hokkien" title="Hokkien">Hokkien</a>, have alternative scripts, namely <a href="/wiki/Cyrillization_of_Chinese" title="Cyrillization of Chinese">Cyrillic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">Latin alphabets</a>. Even between varieties which use Sinographs, characters are repurposed or invented to cover for the difference in vocabulary. Examples include <span lang="zh">靚</span>; &#39;pretty&#39; in Yue,<sup id="cite_ref-guangzhou_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guangzhou-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> <span lang="zh">𠊎</span>; &#39;I&#39;, &#39;me&#39; in Hakka,<sup id="cite_ref-meixian_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meixian-48">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> <span lang="zh">即</span>; &#39;this&#39; in Hokkien,<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> <span lang="zh">覅</span>; &#39;to not want&#39; in Wu,<sup id="cite_ref-shanghai_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shanghai-50">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> <span lang="zh">莫</span>; &#39;do not&#39; in Xiang, and <span lang="zh">嘎</span>; &#39;ill-tempered&#39; in Mandarin.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-harbin_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-harbin-26">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Note that both traditional and simplified characters can be used to write any lect.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Phonology">Phonology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinitic_languages&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Phonology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Phonologically speaking, though all Sinitic languages possess <a href="/wiki/Tone_(linguistics)" title="Tone (linguistics)">tones</a>, their contours and the total number of tones varies wildly, from <a href="/wiki/Shanghainese" title="Shanghainese">Shanghainese</a>, which can be analysed to have only two tones,<sup id="cite_ref-shanghai_50-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shanghai-50">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> to <a href="/wiki/Bobai_dialect" title="Bobai dialect">Bobainese</a>, which has ten.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Sinitic languages also vary wildly in their phonological inventories and phonotactics. Take for instance <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/mɭɤŋ/</span> (<span lang="zh">門兒</span>; &#39;door (diminuitive)&#39;) seen in Pingdingnese,<sup id="cite_ref-diversity_22-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> or <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʃɦɻʷəi/</span> (<span lang="zh">水</span>; &#39;water&#39;) of Xuanzhounese,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> which both show syllables which do not follow the (single) consonant-glide-vowel-consonant syllable structure of more well-known lects. Tone sandhi is also a feature which not all lects share. Cantonese, for instance, only has a very weak system,<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> whereas Wu varieties not only have complex, intricate systems, which affect almost all syllables, but also uses it to mark for grammatical <a href="/wiki/Part_of_speech" title="Part of speech">part of speech</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-shanghai_50-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shanghai-50">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-suzhou_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-suzhou-51">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Take for instance, this simplified analysis of Suzhounese tone sandhi:<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Grammar">Grammar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinitic_languages&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Grammar"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Disregarding phonology, grammar is the feature of Sinitic languages which differ the most. The majority of Sinitic languages do not possess tenses, though exceptions include Northern Wu lects such as Shanghainese and <a href="/wiki/Suzhou_dialect" title="Suzhou dialect">Suzhounese</a>, though it is largely breaking down in Shanghainese due to Mandarin influence.<sup id="cite_ref-suzhou_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-suzhou-51">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Sinitic languages generally also have no case marking, though lects such as Linxianese and Hengshannese do possess case particles, with the latter expressing it through tone change.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Sinitic languages generally have SVO word order and possess classifiers.
</p><p>Verb usage may be different between Sinitic languages. Notice the double verb marking seen in lects such as <a href="/wiki/Beijing_dialect" title="Beijing dialect">Beijingese</a>, in these sentences meaning "today I go to Guangzhou":<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:2em"><div>Beijingese:</div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">今 天</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Jīn tiān</p><p style="margin: 0px;">today</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">我</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">wǒ</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="first person, singular">1sg</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">到</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">dào</p><p style="margin: 0px;">arrive</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">廣 州</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Guǎng zhōu</p><p style="margin: 0px;">Guangzhou</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">去</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">qù</p><p style="margin: 0px;">go</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">&#160;</p><p style="margin: 0px;">(<a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>)</p><p style="margin: 0px;">&#160;</p></div><p style="display: none;">{今 天} 我 到 {廣 州} 去</p><p style="display: none;">{Jīn tiān} wǒ dào {Guǎng zhōu} qù</p><p style="display: none;">today 1sg arrive Guangzhou go</p><p class="mw-empty-elt"></p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:2em"><div>Wuxinese:</div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">今 阿</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">cin<sup>1</sup> - a<sup>1</sup></p><p style="margin: 0px;">today</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">我</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ngeu<sup>4</sup></p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="first person, singular">1sg</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">廣 州</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">kuaon<sup>3</sup> - cieu<sup>1</sup></p><p style="margin: 0px;">Guangzhou</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">去</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">chi<sup>5</sup></p><p style="margin: 0px;">go</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">&#160;</p><p style="margin: 0px;">(<a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Wu_Chinese" title="Romanization of Wu Chinese">Wugniu</a>)</p><p style="margin: 0px;">&#160;</p></div><p style="display: none;">{今 阿} 我 {廣 州} 去</p><p style="display: none;">{cin1 - a1} ngeu4 {kuaon3 - cieu1} chi5</p><p style="display: none;">today 1sg Guangzhou go</p><p class="mw-empty-elt"></p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Indirect_object_marking">Indirect object marking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinitic_languages&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Indirect object marking"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Sinitic languages tend to vary greatly between how they mark indirect objects. The area which varies tends to be the placement of the indirect and direct object.<sup id="cite_ref-other_11-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-other-11">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-diversity_22-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mandarinic, Xiang, Hui and Min languages often place the indirect object (IO) before the direct object (DO). Some lects have switched to IO-DO structure due to Mandarin influence, such as <a href="/wiki/Nanchang_dialect" class="mw-redirect" title="Nanchang dialect">Nanchangese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shanghainese" title="Shanghainese">Shanghainese</a>, though Shanghainese also has the alternative word order.
</p>
<div>
<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;">


<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 50%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:2em"><div>Beijingese:</div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">他</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">tā</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">給</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">gěi</p><p style="margin: 0px;">give</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">了</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">le</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="perfect" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PERF</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">我</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">wǒ</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="first person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">1SG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">一</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">yī</p><p style="margin: 0px;">one</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">盒</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">hé</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="classifier" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">CL</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">糖。</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">táng'</p><p style="margin: 0px;">sweets</p></div><p style="display: none;">他 給 了 我 一 盒 糖。</p><p style="display: none;">tā gěi le wǒ yī hé táng'</p><p style="display: none;">3SG give PERF 1SG one CL sweets</p><p style="clear: left;">"He gave me a box of sweets."</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>

</td>
<td style="width: 50%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:2em"><div>Taiyuanese:</div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">給</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">kei<sup>53</sup></p><p style="margin: 0px;">give</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">我</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ɣə<sup>53</sup></p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="first person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">1SG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">一</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">iəʔ<sup>2</sup></p><p style="margin: 0px;">one</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">本</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">pəŋ<sup>53</sup></p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="classifier" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">CL</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">書。</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">su<sup>11</sup></p><p style="margin: 0px;">book</p></div><p style="display: none;">給 我 一 本 書。</p><p style="display: none;">kei53 ɣə53 iəʔ2 pəŋ53 su11</p><p style="display: none;">give 1SG one CL book</p><p style="clear: left;">"Give me a book."</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>

</p>

<p>On the other hand, Gan, Wu, Hakka, and Yue languages tend to place the DO in front of the IO.
</p>
<div>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Classifiers">Classifiers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinitic_languages&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Classifiers"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Like other East Asian languages such as <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">Korean</a>, Sinitic languages have a system of <a href="/wiki/Classifier_(linguistics)" title="Classifier (linguistics)">classifers</a>, however, use of classifiers vary greatly in features such as <a href="/wiki/Definiteness" title="Definiteness">definiteness</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-diversity_22-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In Cantonese, for instance, they can be used to mark possession, which is rare in Sinitic while common in Southeast Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-other_11-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-other-11">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:2em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">我</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ngo<sup>5</sup></p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="first person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">1SG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">本</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">bun<sup>2</sup></p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="classifier" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">CL</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">書</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">syu<sup>1</sup></p><p style="margin: 0px;">book</p></div><p style="display: none;">我 本 書</p><p style="display: none;">ngo5 bun2 syu1</p><p style="display: none;">1SG CL book</p><p style="clear: left;">'my book'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<p><span lang="zh">個</span> and <span lang="zh">隻</span> are the most common generic classifiers cross-linguistically.<sup id="cite_ref-other_11-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-other-11">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> As previously mentioned, Mandarinic languages tend to have fewer classifiers whereas the Southern non-Mandarinic varieties tend to have more.<sup id="cite_ref-diversity_22-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Demonstratives">Demonstratives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinitic_languages&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Demonstratives"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Sinitic languages can vary greatly in their system of <a href="/wiki/Demonstratives" class="mw-redirect" title="Demonstratives">demonstratives</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-diversity_22-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Standard_Mandarin" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard Mandarin">Standard Mandarin</a> and other Northeastern varieties has a two-way system: <span lang="zh">這</span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn">zhè</span></i> (proximal) and <span lang="zh">那</span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn">nà</span></i> (distal), but this is not the only system found in Sinitic languages.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Wuhan_dialect" title="Wuhan dialect">Wuhannese</a> has a neutral demonstrative, which can be used regardless of the distance to the deitic center.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Similar systems are found in Northern Wu lects such as Suzhounese and <a href="/wiki/Ningbo_dialect" title="Ningbo dialect">Ningbonese</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-suzhou_51-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-suzhou-51">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-diversity_22-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:2em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><sup id="cite_ref-wuhan_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wuhan-88">&#91;c&#93;</a></sup></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">nɤ<sup>35</sup></p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="demonstrative" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">DEM</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">是</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">sɿ<sup>35</sup></p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="copula" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">COP</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">生</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">sən<sup>55</sup></p><p style="margin: 0px;">unripe</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">的</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ti</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="patient-like argument of canonical transitive verb">P</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">，</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">&#160;</p><p style="margin: 0px;">&#160;</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;"><sup id="cite_ref-wuhan_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wuhan-88">&#91;c&#93;</a></sup></p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">nɤ<sup>35</sup></p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="demonstrative" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">DEM</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">是</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">sɿ<sup>35</sup></p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="copula" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">COP</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">熟</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">səu<sup>213</sup></p><p style="margin: 0px;">ripe</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;">的</p><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ti</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="patient-like argument of canonical transitive verb">P</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;"><sup id="cite_ref-wuhan_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wuhan-88">&#91;c&#93;</a></sup> 是 生 的 ， <sup id="cite_ref-wuhan_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wuhan-88">&#91;c&#93;</a></sup> 是 熟 的</p><p style="display: none;">nɤ35 sɿ35 sən55 ti {} nɤ35 sɿ35 səu213 ti</p><p style="display: none;">DEM COP unripe P {} DEM COP ripe P</p><p class="mw-empty-elt"></p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<p>In the above sentence, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/nɤ³⁵/</span> can be translated as both 'this' and 'that'. Though Wuhannese has this system of a one-term neutral system, it also has a two-way proximal-distal system. This is same for most other lects with a one-term system.
</p><p>Even within two-way systems, which is the most common system, terms could have developed to mean the opposite distance from the deitic center. Cantonese <span lang="zh">嗰</span>; <i><span lang="yue-Latn-jyutping">go²</span></i> (distal) and Shanghainese <span lang="zh">搿</span>; <i><span lang="yue-Latn-jyutping">geq</span></i> (proximal) are both etymologically from <span lang="zh">個</span>, for instance.<sup id="cite_ref-guangzhou_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guangzhou-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-shanghai_50-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shanghai-50">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Many Sinitic languages have three-way systems, but the three distances are not always the same ones. For instance, whereas Guangshan Mandarin has a person-oriented proximal, medial, distal system, Xinyu Gan has a distance-oriented close, proximal, distal system. Gan especially has many varieties with a three-way system, sometimes even marked with tone and vowel length rather than just changing the term used.<sup id="cite_ref-diversity_22-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A small number of varieties possess even four- or five-term demonstrative systems. Take for instance the following:<sup id="cite_ref-diversity_22-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diversity-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align: center" cellpadding="5">
<tbody><tr>
<th></th>
<th>Dongxiang</th>
<th>Zhangshu
</th></tr>
<tr>
<th>Close
</th>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">꜀ko</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">kọ꜆</span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>Proximal
</th>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">꜁ko</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ko꜆</span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>Distal
</th>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">꜀e</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">꜃hɛ</span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>Yonder
</th>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">꜁e</span></td>
<td><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">꜃hɛ̣</span>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>These two lects use tone change and vowel length respectively to distinguish between the four demonstratives.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinitic_languages&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Notes"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">From Late Latin <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/S%C4%ABnae" class="extiw" title="wikt:Sīnae">Sīnae</a></i>, "the Chinese", probably from Arabic <i>Ṣīn</i> ('China'), from the Chinese dynastic name <a href="/wiki/Qin_dynasty" title="Qin dynasty">Qin</a>. (<i><a href="/wiki/OED" class="mw-redirect" title="OED">OED</a></i>). In 1982, <a href="/wiki/Paul_K._Benedict" title="Paul K. Benedict">Paul K. Benedict</a> proposed a subgroup of Sino-Tibetan called "Sinitic" comprising <a href="/wiki/Bai_language" title="Bai language">Bai</a> and Chinese.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWang2005107_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWang2005107-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The precise affiliation of Bai remains uncertain<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWang2005122_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWang2005122-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> and the term "Sinitic" is usually used as a synonym for Chinese, especially when viewed as a language family rather than as a language.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMair19913_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMair19913-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">See, for example, <a href="#CITEREFEnfield2003">Enfield (2003</a>:69) and <a href="#CITEREFHannas1997">Hannas (1997)</a>. The Chinese terms often translated as 'language' and 'dialect' do not correspond well to those translations. These are <span lang="zh">語言</span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn">yǔyán</span></i>, corresponding to <a href="/wiki/Macrolanguage" class="mw-redirect" title="Macrolanguage">macrolanguage</a> or <a href="/wiki/Language_cluster" class="mw-redirect" title="Language cluster">language cluster</a>, which is used for Chinese itself; <span lang="zh">方言</span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn">fāngyán</span></i>, which separates mutually unintelligible languages within a <i><span lang="zh-Latn">yǔyán</span></i>; and <span lang="zh">土語</span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn">tǔyǔ</span></i> or <span lang="zh">土話</span>; <i><span lang="zh-Latn">tǔhuà</span></i>, which corresponds better to the familiar Western linguistic use of 'dialect'.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBradley20121_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBradley20121-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-wuhan-88"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-wuhan_88-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-wuhan_88-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">This term was not assigned a character.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
